Depositary's Acknowledgment of Heir and the Binding Effect of Istishab
Ruling with proof and comparative analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a depositary's acknowledgment of an heir and apply the principle of istishab al-hal to similar cases.

Core Idea
A depositary's acknowledgment of a sole heir binds him: later acknowledgments do not revoke the first.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a depositary states that a particular person is the deceased's only son and sole heir. The ruling is clear: he must give the deposit to that son, and even if he later acknowledges another son, the first remains entitled. The commentary expands on the underlying proof, invoking the principle of istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) and contrasting it with Zufar's view on a related inheritance issue. The discussion also distinguishes cases where acknowledgment is effective from those where it is not, such as acknowledging an agent during the owner's lifetime.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
Read the opening: the depositary says 'this is the son of the depositor, he has no other heir.' The ruling is that he must give the deposit to that son. Note the key phrase: 'وَلَوْ أَقَرَّ بِابْنٍ آخَرَ ... فَهِيَ لَهُ' — even if he later acknowledges another son and denies the first, the deposit remains for the first.
This is a direct legal statement (matn).
2
Understand the proof for the ruling
The commentary explains the basis: the depositary's acknowledgment establishes that the property in his hand belongs to the heir as successor to the deceased. This is analogous to acknowledging ownership during the owner's life. The proof relies on the principle of istishab al-hal: the present state (the cause of deprivation being established now) is projected back to the past as a defensive proof.
The proof is 'dalīl 'aqlī' (rational evidence) grounded in legal presumption.
3
Contrast with Zufar's view on a related case
The commentary brings Zufar's disagreement on a separate inheritance case: a wife converts to Islam after her husband's death and claims inheritance. Zufar says her word is taken because events are attributed to the nearest time (so her conversion is considered after death, making her Muslim at death). The Hanafi response: the present (istishab) only suffices for defense (دفع), not for establishing entitlement (استحقاق). The wife needs entitlement, which requires stronger evidence.
This contrast illustrates the limited scope of istishab in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the distinction to other scenarios in the text
The passage contrasts three cases: (a) depositary acknowledging an heir → acceptable (after death). (b) depositary acknowledging an agent to take possession during owner's life → not accepted, as it invalidates the owner's right (المودع حي). (c) debtor acknowledging an agent to collect the debt → accepted, because the debtor acknowledges his own obligation; debts are repaid by equivalents, so no specific property is invalidated.
The key distinction: acknowledgment affecting another's right vs. acknowledging one's own obligation.
5
Confirm the muftā bihī and practical consequence
The Hanafi position is that the first acknowledged son gets the deposit. This is the relied-upon view (muftā bihī). The practical consequence is that a depositary cannot later change the beneficiary by acknowledging another heir.
There is no intra-Hanafi dispute on this specific ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال : هذا ابن مودعي الميت لا وارث له غيرُه دَفَعَها إليه ، ولو أقر بابن آخر لمودعيه ، وجحد الأول، فهي له
هذا عندنا ، وعند زفرَ الله في المسألة الأولى القول قولها ؛ لأنَّ الإسلام حادث فيضافُ إلى أقرب الأوقات، ولنا : أن سبب الحرمان ثابت في الحال، فيثبت فيما مضى تحكيماً للحال") ، وهي تَصْلُحُ حجَّةً للدفع "[0] (ومن قال : هذا ابنُ مودعي الميت لا وارث له غيرُه دَفَعَها إليه) : أي دفع الوديعة إليه ، ولو أقر بابن آخر المودعه، وجحد الأول، فهي له) [١) قوله : لأن الإسلام ... الخ ؛ حاصله أنَّ الإسلام حادث، والأصل في الحوادث أن تضاف إلى أقرب أوقاته، وأقرب أوقاته ما بعد الموت فيضاف إليه. [٢]قوله : تحكيماً للحال ؛ أي باستصحاب الحال، كما في جريان ماء الطاحونة ، فإنَّ أيها مع المستأجر إذا اختلفا بعد مضي المدة في جريان الماء وانقطاعه، يُحَكِّمُ الحال، فإن كان جارياً في الحال كان القولُ قول ربِّ الطاحونة ، وإن لم يكن جارياً كان القولُ قول المستأجر. [٣] قوله : وهي تصلح حجة للدفع ؛ وما ذكره زفر الله هو يعتبر للاستحقاق، والظاهر لا يصلح للاستحقاق، ويصلح للدفع. [٤] قوله : ومن قال...الخ ؛ يعني إذا مات رجلٌ ولـه عـنـد رجـل وديعة ، فقال المستودع : هذا ابن الميت لا وارث له غيرُه ، فإنّه يجب عليه دفع المال إليه ؛ لإقراره بأنّ ما في يده ملك الوارث خلافةٌ عن الميت، فصار كما إذا أقر أنه ملك المورث، وهو حي أصالة. بخلاف ما إذا أقر لرجل أنه وكيل المودع بالقبض ، وأنه اشتراه منه، حيث لا يؤمرُ بالدفع إليه ؛ لأنَّ فيه إبطال حق المودع في العين بإزالتها عن يده ؛ لأن يد المودع كيد المالك ، فلا يقبلُ إقراره عليه، ولا كذلك بعد موته. (1) بخلاف المدين إذا أقر أنه وكيل الطالب بقبض دينه ، حيث يؤمر بالدفع إليه ؛ لأنه إقرار بخالص حقه ؛ إذ الديون تقضى بأمثالها فيؤمرُ بالدَّفع إليه كذا في «التبيين» [ 0 ] قوله : ولو أقر ... الخ ؛ يعني إذا قال مودعُ الميت لرجل آخر بعدما أقر للأول :
And whoever says: 'This is the son of the depositor of the deceased, he has no heir other than him,' he gives it to him [the son]. And if he acknowledged another son of the depositor and denied the first, it is for him [the first]. This is our view. And according to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, in the first issue, the word is hers [the wife's] because Islam is an event and is attributed to the nearest time. And for us: the cause of deprivation is established in the present, so it is established in the past by making the case judge by the present. And it [the present] is suitable as a proof for defense. [0] His statement: 'And whoever said...' means: he gives the deposit to him. And if he acknowledged another son of the depositor and denied the first, it is for him [the first]. [1] The gist of 'because Islam...': that Islam is an event, and the principle for events is that they are attributed to their nearest times, and its nearest time is after death, so it is attributed to it. [2] His statement: 'making the case judge by the present' means by istishab al-hal, as in the flow of the mill's water: if the mill owner and the tenant differ after the period about the flow and stoppage, the present is used. If it is flowing now, the word of the mill owner is taken; if not, the word of the tenant. [3] His statement: 'It is suitable as proof for defense' – what Zufar mentioned considers entitlement, but the apparent is not suitable for entitlement and is suitable for defense. [4] His statement: 'And whoever said...' means: if a man dies and has a deposit with a man, and the depositary says: 'This is the son of the deceased, he has no heir other than him,' it is obligatory for him to give the property to him because of his acknowledgment that what is in his hand is the property of the heir as a successor from the deceased. So it becomes as if he acknowledged that it belonged to the testator while he was alive originally. Contrary to if he acknowledged to a man that he was the agent of the depositor in taking possession and that he bought it from him, then he is not ordered to give it to him because it involves invalidating the depositor's right in the property by removing it from his hand, because the hand of the depositor is like the hand of the owner. So his acknowledgment is not accepted against him, unlike after his death. Contrary to the debtor if he acknowledges that he is the agent of the creditor in receiving his debt, where he is ordered to give it to him because it is an acknowledgment of his pure right, for debts are repaid by their equivalents, so he is ordered to give it to him. This is in al-Tabyin. [0] His statement: 'And if he acknowledged...' means: when the depositor of the deceased says to another man after he acknowledged to the first...
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that a depositary must give the deposit to a son he acknowledges as the sole heir, and if later he acknowledges another son, the first retains the right. The commentary then references Zufar's disagreement on the earlier inheritance issue, using it to illustrate the istishab principle. The commentary explains that the depositary's acknowledgment is binding because the property belongs to the heir by succession, and the acknowledgment does not harm the original owner's right after death. It contrasts with the case of acknowledging an agent to receive the property during the owner's life, which would invalidate the owner's right. It also compares with the debtor acknowledging an agent to collect the debt, which is valid because the debtor's acknowledgment is of his own obligation. The passage ends with an incomplete explanation about acknowledging a second son.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; in this context, the depositary's statement that a person is the heir, which is binding and obligates him to give the deposit.
وديعة (wadi'ah): Deposit; a contract where property is entrusted to someone for safekeeping. The depositary must return it to the owner or his heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, if a depositary first acknowledges one son as the sole heir and later acknowledges another son, who gets the deposit?
A) The second son, because the later acknowledgment supersedes the first.
B) Both sons share equally.
C) The first son alone gets it.
D) The deposit goes to the state.

Key Takeaway
A depositary's acknowledgment of an heir is binding and irrevocable; the first acknowledged heir retains the deposit even if a later acknowledgment contradicts it.
